I think I&#x27;ve only charged it once in almost 2 months of use.&lt;br /&gt;i also like the improvement in the head/blade removal - it is hinged, so I wont drop it into a trash can ever again trying to shake the stubble out.&lt;br /&gt;I hope it lasts as long as my old one did!</li>

Also, I have to press the razor very hard on my face in order to shave the stubble AND IT LEAVES MY SKIN FEELING LIKE I SHAVED WITH SANDPAPER. Even my old shaver which was half the price of this new one used to do a better and faster job in half the time. I WOULD NOT RECOMMEND IT FOR THOSE FELLAS WITH A LOT OF FACIAL HAIR. The instructions say give it three weeks minimum to adjust to the new system.  They&#x27;re serious.  My first few shaves were very discouraging, slow, uncomfortable, uneven, and I was left with red irritated skin under my chin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I tried various pre-shaves and aftershaves. By three weeks, I saw large improvements, but I still wasn&#x27;t sure.  It&#x27;s seven weeks, now, and I&#x27;m very impressed.  I get a quick close and comfortable shave, and It&#x27;s still improving.  I&#x27;m glad I made the switch.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;FYI&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - I only shave twice a week&lt;br /&gt; - My whiskers are pretty coarse and heavy&lt;br /&gt; - I settled on soaking my face with hot water then applying liquid hand soap as my pre-shave routine.  It works really well to make the razor glide over my skin.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; - I use Bulldog After shave Balm but am feeling the need for it less and less(I hadn&#x27;t used aftershave almost ever with the blade)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;------&lt;br /&gt;Update:&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s now ten weeks, and I gave up on this razor. I hope it can handle the stubble better.</li>

    <li> My Norelco arrived 2 days earlier than the estimated date which was a welcome surprise. I have not used an electric shaver since the 70&#x27;s when I received one as a gift. Apparently, the technology from those days just didn&#x27;t cut the mustard and I was back to using a blade just a few short months later. I had never really considered going back to an electric shaver until I was forced to undergo carotid artery surgery which left a nasty scar from my jawbone to near my collarbone. I can&#x27;t express the challenge of trying to get a blade close to that sensitive area not to mention I suffered some nerve damage on the surrounding scar tissue as well, adding to the painful task.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Reading through many of the reviews on a number of different Norelco models, I settled with this particular razor and I can&#x27;t tell you enough of how pleased I am with my purchase. This PT730 actually shaves better than a blade and those tough areas are now a breeze to whisk over. I&#x27;ve gone for several days without a shave and this model does not discriminate against the length of the whiskers. The added pop-up trimmer is very efficient in trimming my sideburns and moustache to boot.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While the instruction booklet discusses a break-in period and possible facial irritation during the adjustment time, I have not been affected in the least and there is no pulling effect felt at all, just a smooth comfortable shave. Clean up is a snap and the convenience of cordless operation makes this Norelco a product I would highly recommend!</li>
    <li> I don&#x27;t know about you but my electric razors seem to last three or four years and then it&#x27;s time to toss them. This is the case for the replacement I currently and. Even the rotary blades wills et you back almost as much as a new razor. I researched all of the Norelco razor and found you can spend a lot of money for the upper end models. Im opted to stay closest to the bottom and just continue to tossing them as they wear out. This one does a good job of shaving mainly because the unit and the blades are still new.i</li>

    <li> I can&#x27;t really compare it to other electric razors, but it definitely doesn&#x27;t cut as close as a manual one.     <li> For facial hair, it cuts really close, but sometimes have to shave over once with a disposable razor blade to rid of the very few strands of shortened hair that remain, in order to keep my face extra smooth. I use it to tidy up my beard while also keeping it low, to keep my mustache a certain length, and to shave my sides off, once a week. Each session takes about 3 - 5 minutes.    As for head hair, I have not used it to cut as close to the scalp as possible. I do use it to keep my hair low though (usually between 5mm to 10mm). One minor problem I have with shaving my head with this shaver is since my hair is very curly, after one pass around my whole head I have to clean out the shaver, or else the cut hair will curl around the blades, causing them to spin slower and cut inefficiently. Sometimes my hair gets stuck between a few grooves, which slightly extends the time to clean. To reduce the time spent stopping to clean the shaver out, I try not to go more than 2 days without shaving my head. Each session takes about 10 - 15 minutes, not including the time it takes to clean out the item (which would double the time).    When kept clean, the Philips Norelco PT730/41 Shaver 3500 cuts hair very well. If completely dead, it takes about 8 hours to fully charge, as indicated on the box. I usually charge it while I sleep after I&#x27;ve used it for about four 5-10 minute sessions. I&#x27;ve had this product for about 2 and a half months now and it works the same as it did when I first used it.</li>

    <li> Philips PT730 Razor&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This cordless razor was tested on whiskers that were used to an old fashioned blade shaver. All test shaving has been done on dry skin.     <li> The Norelco PT730 shaves very closely. In comparison with a 10-year old Norelco model (fitted with brand new blades), it leaves the face much smoother. This is probably due to the modifications that have been made to the circular screens that contact the skin. The ability to rinse the shaver under running water is a great convenience.  Here are a couple of tips for maintenance:  *As recommended in the product manual, do rinse the blade assembly and parts where the hair collects after each use. After rinsing and gently shaking to remove dripping water, leave the head assembly open to air dry. Be careful when shaking the unit, as the head assembly is held by a friction spring, and can easily be shaken apart from the razor body.  *While it is possible to disassemble the head assembly for brush cleaning, the reassembly is not as straightforward as was the case with earlier models, so you want to avoid having to do this until necessary.  These razors have come down in price over the years, have a better battery (lithium-ion vs. nickel-cadmium), and do a better job. If you have an older Norelco razor, you might consider replacing it with the PT730.</li>

    <li> This is my first rotating-head-style shaver. The biggest issue for me with electric shavers is that my beard is light -- I only need to shave a few times a week -- and my innate laziness about shaving regularly leaves me with isolated stubble that&#x27;s grown so long it usually folds beneath the foil of a shaver and never gets chopped off.  Which forces me to shave with a razor and foam to get back to a clean-shaven face.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The rotating-head shaving experience is definitely odd.  In particular, I find this shaver isn&#x27;t especially good at getting stubble just below my nose ... conventional straight-foil shavers seem to do that better.  (I&#x27;ve since learned to adjust how I hold the shaver to get that nasally challenged beard.)  And, to be honest, I&#x27;m not really sure how good it is getting stubble that&#x27;s grown to a certain length because the shaver&#x27;s reliability on a single charge has prompted me to shave more often.  (Recent experience suggests it *does* do better than my previous shavers at chopping off longer stubble.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Still, I seem to get a half-dozen shaves on a single charge, and the shaver thoughtfully uses the charging light as a warning signal -- ordinarily off when not being charged, it will start to flash when the charge is running low.  It&#x27;s also surprisingly quiet.  The first time I used it I was afraid I hadn&#x27;t charged it long enough, but in the absence of other evidence I&#x27;ve concluded that the rotating-head system appears to require less horsepower from the motor, which means I can actually listen to the radio while shaving in the morning ... a good thing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, overall, I&#x27;m satisfied and can certainly recommend this Philips Norelco to anyone with a light beard like mine.     <li> I have been very pleased with the PT730 after one month. In doing research before purchasing the shaver, I took all  the posted reviews, both positive and negative,  with a grain of salt. A user&#x27;s impressions will be based on various factors.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1. Type of beard: I consider my beard to be a solid medium to slightly heavy. I have stubble every day and if I don&#x27;t shave for 2 days, it starts to look grubby. I&#x27;ve had no problems getting a fairly close shave where the skin feels smooth when I run my hand on it afterwards. Daily shaving is my routine.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. Expectations: Rotary shavers do required more passes then foil shavers. I expect that I will have to make more passes than a foil shaver, or a high end rotary shaver. I use a mixture of shaving motions -- circular, sideways and vertical against the grain. This has worked well. I also use a fairly light touch so the shaver heads glide and don&#x27;t pinch the stubble.  While it is recommended by experienced users and Philips Norelco that the user shave exclusively with the shaver for 3-4 weeks to get the skin acclimated, I had no break-in period right from the start. This may be due in part to shaving every day, using a light touch and the variety of shaving motions.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3. Quiet, slow speed: I don&#x27;t have any other shaver to compare this with; however, I go by results. The shaver doesn&#x27;t have a high revolution sound to it and is fairly quiet; however, the results on my daily stubble growth have been satisfactory. so when people complain about the slow speed and sound of the motor, I take that with a grain of salt. The shaver does get the job done.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4: On durability of shaver and cutters: I&#x27;ll have to wait a year before I determine how long the cutting heads last. I am though, cleaning them daily and lubricating/degreasing them once a week. I am doing a dry clean only without rinsing the heads under water. This does take a few minutes, to carefully remove the cutting heads and the cutters from the combs; however, I don&#x27;t spend any more time than I would with a normal razor where I  pre-wash my face and lather on shaving cream.  I expect that how long I can use the cutting heads will be dependent on the thickness of my beard, the design/manufacture of the cutters, and the care I take of the shaver. If I find the cutters getting dull within a year, then I my satisfaction level may change.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5. Battery: I&#x27;m getting nearly 3 weeks of shaving before I need to charge the shaver. Again, I expect that this will decrease over time through battery wear.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Other considerations in my purchase: I&#x27;m going to be living overseas. I wanted a shaver that could be used either cordless or with cord. Higher priced wet/dry shavers tend to run on battery only after charging and cannot be used with cord. I was also concerned about cost. Foil shavers seem to have higher blade and foil replacement costs, as do the cleaning system cartridges for high end models. Budget was a consideration. The approximate $25 cost for the replacement HQ8 cutters seems reasonable when compared with replacement costs for other shavers. It&#x27;s still, though an expense to consider down the road.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I realize that uses with extremely heavy beards may or may not find the PT730 acceptable. For me, the PT730 has more than fulfilled my expectations for a low to medium range shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s getting close to one year since my purchase and I want to comment on the status of the cutter blades. It is definitely taking longer to get a close shave, yet I feel no pinching when shaving. I still find it more convenient, even taking a longer time, to not have to wet and lather my face and using an old fashioned razor with the expensive replacement blades, despite this shaver not giving as close a shave as a razor. The results I get, though are still acceptable. The manufacturer&#x27;s advice to replace the blades yearly may be accurate. A few things to keep in mind, whichmay have affected the blades lasting this long.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) I always do a dry clean after shaving and do not run the shaver under water.&lt;br /&gt;2) I use the Norelco cleaning spray once a week.&lt;br /&gt;3) I put a few drops of oil on the cutter blades once a week.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;--------------------------------------------&lt;br /&gt;Second Update:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s a little over one year. Longer shaving times -- 5 minutes or so for a light growth of 1-2 days. Yet again, there is no pinching. I haven&#x27;t replaced the cutter blades, but may in a few months. I would still highly recommend this, one year later.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Third Update:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s been over two years and I just changed the cutter blades -- long overdue. Until I did, it took more than five minutes to shave. Under the chin with longer hairs was more difficult. I had to repeatedly go over the same area countless times. Still, though, no nicking. With the new cutter blades, it&#x27;s like new. Battery is still holding a charge.and do not run the shaver under water. 2) I use the Norelco cleaning spray once a week. 3) I put a few drops of oil on the cutter blades once a week.  -------------------------------------------- Second Update:  It&#x27;s a little over one year. Longer shaving times -- 5 minutes or so for a light growth of 1-2 days. Yet again, there is no pinching. I haven&#x27;t replaced the cutter blades, but may in a few months. I would still highly recommend this, one year later.    Third Update:  It&#x27;s been over two years and I just changed the cutter blades -- long overdue. Until I did, it took more than five minutes to shave. Under the chin with longer hairs was more difficult. I had to repeatedly go over the same area countless times. Still, though, no nicking. With the new cutter blades, it&#x27;s like new. Battery is still holding a charge.</li>

    <li> My intent for the purchase of an electric razor is to replace shaving my face and head with a straight razor. This electric razor does a good job shaving my head and a mediocre job face and neck. I attribute this to having different types of hair. I have straight and slightly thick hair on my head and thick and curly facial hair. I find shaving dry I only need to make 3 to 4 pass on my head and 2 to 3 with electric razor liquid. The resulting cut is the same. It almost a smooth shave, but you can feel a little stubble. At the end of the day, my head is pretty much velcro. I imagine if you have really thick hair, you may have problems getting it shaved with this. If I let my hair go for a few days, I have to make numerous passes and I can hear the motor struggling.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;On my face and neck, I have to make numerous passes and there are always a few hairs that just don&#x27;t get picked up. Always been the case no matter which electric razors I&#x27;ve used in the past.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A few things to note, the head just warm up rather quickly and I find it affects the shaving. As other reviews mention, the motor does seem rather weak. This razor is best for maintaining a clean shave everyday, rather than shaving every other day or so. What works best for me is to keep it by my desk, and whenever I check my work email before heading out to work, I&#x27;ll shave my head and face. Even if I miss a spot or two, it is not really noticeable and I&#x27;ll get it when I get home or make a note to make a pass in the morning. Works for me! A full charge lasts me about a week, but I use it significantly longer during shaves.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cleaning is simple. Open the head, tap against the sink, and rinse with water. It comes with a brush for the hair that is just stuck. Easy process.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For face shaving, I&#x27;d give it a 3/5.&lt;br /&gt;For head shaving, I&#x27;d give it a 4/5. (As long as you shave daily) I&#x27;m taking 1 point off because of the motor being easily strained and not being able to take thickerhair well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Ultimately, if you purchase this to replace razor shaving, you&#x27;ll be disappointed if you care about shave quality. I stopped caring about having a silky smooth head and this is a happy middle ground for convenience and somewhat smooth. I fully expect to shave with my straight razor every now and then in the future, but in the meantime, this fits my bill and I&#x27;m happy with it as I wasn&#x27;t expecting it to do decently on facial hair.</li>

    <li> Works well.  Happy with purchase.</li>
    <li> It&#x27;s been over 10 years since I regularly used an electric razor. I&#x27;ve owned at least 6 electrics of various brands and types (rotary, foil, etc.) over the years, and have always returned to using a blade after 6 months or so. I would always get tired of the skin irritation, the poor, uneven closeness of the shave, and the length of time a reasonably close shave would take. But I figured it&#x27;s been 10 years since I last tried one, and wet razors have made tremendous advances in closeness and comfort, maybe electrics have gotten better, too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I didn&#x27;t want to spend a fortune on an electric razor, but I also didn&#x27;t want the bottom end of the product line, so I went with the Norelco PT730 as it seems to offer some higher-end feature like a rechargeable Lithium-Ion battery, the \\&quot;Super Lift &amp; Cut\\&quot; blade system (which promises to offer a closer shave with less irritation), a built-in trimmer, and a fully washable design (which I was very interested in).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Not all that much has changed with electrics in the past 10 years. Same basic shape and \\&quot;floating\\&quot; rotary blade layout as my last Norelco (no idea of the model number). They added some nice looking trim stripes, grippy surfaces, and ergonomic curves to the body, so it&#x27;s easier to hold onto. And it&#x27;s A LOT lighter than I remember my old one being. Probably a combination of the Lithium Ion battery and a lot more plastic parts - but that&#x27;s what you get today no matter what you buy. The \\&quot;controls\\&quot; (on/off, and trimmer) are easy to reach and activate, and have a quality feel like they will last for awhile.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I followed the directions and charged up the unit until the charging light lit up continuously (took roughly overnight). The next morning when I went to use it for the first time, I was struck just how quiet the shaver is in operation. I could probably use this in the master bathroom with the door closed and not wake my sleeping girlfriend. I was also worried that it was so quiet that it lacked the necessary power to do the job. Fortunately, I was worried for nothing because it powered through my 2 day beard growth without slowing noticeably. I didn&#x27;t have very high expectations for a close shave that first day because I needed to get used to using an electric razor again. Like every manufacturer warns in their owners manual, Philips Norelco has the standard disclaimer: \\&quot;Your skin may need 2 or 3 weeks to get accustomed to the Philips shaving system\\&quot;. I did however, find the shaver easy to hold and manipulate around the curves of my face. I got a decent shave, though no where near as close as a razor shave. It&#x27;s always a good idea to freshly wash your face just prior to shaving. This removes the facial oils that clog up a razor, and lifts the whiskers off your face for a closer shave. It&#x27;s VERY IMPORTANT to thoroughly dry your face first before using the razor as the moisture on your skin will cause the heads to drag making shaving most frustrating. They offer alcohol based pre-shave products that clean and dry your face faster than air alone. These can dry out the skin though.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve been using the shaver roughly every other day now for just about a month. I&#x27;ve gotten very comfortable with directing the razor over the different areas of my face. My beard grows very flat on my neck and requires many many passes in different directions to obtain a close shave. Just like every other electric razor I have owned this inevitably causes burning and irritation in that area after each shave.  Shaving this area on my neck is probably the biggest reason I don&#x27;t usually use an electric.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Shaving my cheeks and jaw worked fairly well and I got a close shave in those areas after a few passes - not much irritation at all. I wear a goatee and getting in close around the edge of my facial hair was not easy. The circular blades have a border around them that attaches them to the shaver body. This border makes it somewhat difficult to get in close to the edge of my goatee and resulted in some light stubble remaining around the border of my goatee. The goal with well trimmed facial hair is a very close shave around this border which makes the goatee look very neat and sculpted. To be fair, this sharp, clean border is even difficult with a wet razor and requires practice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;After shaving I love that I can just flip up the heads and rinse them off with hot water. Saves a lot of aggravation. I have a small spray bottle of alcohol that I spritz on the heads afterward to speed drying. (You&#x27;re supposed to let the heads dry before closing them back up.) They state in the manual: \\&quot;For the best cleaning results, we advise you to use the Philips Cleaning spray (HQ110).\\&quot; This stuff is basically alcohol with a bit of mineral oil in a spray can for 6 buck or so. Save your money.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I used the trimmer function a few times to \\&quot;pre-shave\\&quot; my beard when it was especially long after 3 or 4 days growth. It did trim my long whiskers somewhat but is under-powered for the job. I ended up using my Norelco beard trimmer to finish the job, as it is designed for this kind of work. The trimmer also does a lack-luster job at trimming the edges of my goatee and sideburns. But to be fair it is just as bad as every other built-in trimmer I&#x27;ve used in the past - so I&#x27;m not deducting any points for this.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I didn&#x27;t actually time my shaves but I estimate it takes me 5 to 7 minutes roughly every other day to get a close shave. I guess I got 3 - 4 full power shaves between each 8 hour recharge. I was running out of juice near the end of one shave and I plugged the unit in to finish it. A bit more awkward with the cord but it&#x27;s nice to know you won&#x27;t get stuck running out of power in the middle of a shave when you&#x27;re late for work! You can also do a quick 3 minute charge for 5 minutes of cordless shaving, though I didn&#x27;t try this.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Not surprisingly, I still prefer the closeness and lack of irritation of a high quality 5-blade wet razor. And as usual because I have to spend so long repeatedly going over the same areas of my beard to get a close shave, there is really no time savings (for me) with an electric razor. But as far as electrics go the Philips Norelco PT730 PowerTouch Rechargeable Cordless Razor is a very nice product at a reasonable price point (I spent more for my last Norelco 10 years ago!). I found the ability to just flip-up the shaving heads and rinse them under hot water to be a real time saver, and it kept the razor performing much better between thorough cleanings involving disassembly of the heads.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All in all, I can recommend this product as a very good choice in electric razors at a fair price for the features and performance.e remaining around the border of my goatee. The goal with well trimmed facial hair is a very close shave around this border which makes the goatee look very neat and sculpted. To be fair, this sharp, clean border is even difficult with a wet razor and requires practice.  After shaving I love that I can just flip up the heads and rinse them off with hot water. Saves a lot of aggravation. I have a small spray bottle of alcohol that I spritz on the heads afterward to speed drying. (You&#x27;re supposed to let the heads dry before closing them back up.) They state in the manual: \\&quot;For the best cleaning results, we advise you to use the Philips Cleaning spray (HQ110).\\&quot; This stuff is basically alcohol with a bit of mineral oil in a spray can for 6 buck or so. Save your money.  I used the trimmer function a few times to \\&quot;pre-shave\\&quot; my beard when it was especially long after 3 or 4 days growth. It did trim my long whiskers somewhat but is under-powered for the job. I ended up using my Norelco beard trimmer to finish the job, as it is designed for this kind of work. The trimmer also does a lack-luster job at trimming the edges of my goatee and sideburns. But to be fair it is just as bad as every other built-in trimmer I&#x27;ve used in the past - so I&#x27;m not deducting any points for this.  I didn&#x27;t actually time my shaves but I estimate it takes me 5 to 7 minutes roughly every other day to get a close shave. I guess I got 3 - 4 full power shaves between each 8 hour recharge. I was running out of juice near the end of one shave and I plugged the unit in to finish it. A bit more awkward with the cord but it&#x27;s nice to know you won&#x27;t get stuck running out of power in the middle of a shave when you&#x27;re late for work! You can also do a quick 3 minute charge for 5 minutes of cordless shaving, though I didn&#x27;t try this.  Not surprisingly, I still prefer the closeness and lack of irritation of a high quality 5-blade wet razor. And as usual because I have to spend so long repeatedly going over thesame areas of my beard to get a close shave, there is really no time savings (for me) with an electric razor. But as far as electrics go the Philips Norelco PT730 PowerTouch Rechargeable Cordless Razor is a very nice product at a reasonable price point (I spent more for my last Norelco 10 years ago!). I found the ability to just flip-up the shaving heads and rinse them under hot water to be a real time saver, and it kept the razor performing much better between thorough cleanings involving disassembly of the heads.  All in all, I can recommend this product as a very good choice in electric razors at a fair price for the features and performance.</li>

    <li> After much deliberation, I decided to try this Phillips Norelco PT730 Razor, if only for the reason that it could be used while plugged in.  Previously I&#x27;d had an inexpensive foil razor from Panasonic that I liked very much, but the foil broke and the replacement costs were more than the razor itself.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I bought the PT730 to shave my scalp. The end result is that on more than one occasion I&#x27;ve taken huge chunks of my scalp out with one of these fifty-seven blade monstrosities that Schick and Gillette put out.  You&#x27;ve never known pain until you put a styptic pencil on a gaping wound in your head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So bring on the Norelco PT730.  First impressions were a bit shaky. I used it on my face, and there were some small razor burns and pulls, but nothing like a previous rotary razor I had a few years back.  The flexible heads do a great job of fitting the contours of the face.  Clean up was easy, just a rinse, a shake, and some time to dry.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some have argued the razor feels cheap, and it does appear that the accessories, namely the plug and the protective cover for the blades, are cheaper.  The power cord is a thin cord that looks to be made out of the same wire as a USB cable.  But I was glad to see that Norelco didn&#x27;t coil the cord.  This allows you to use it plugged in at a much further distance from the wall.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I cannot yet speak to charge times or usage time but it seems as though the stated 8 hours charge and 40 minute usage are about right.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you&#x27;re a bald guy who needs a steady solution to shaving your head, I highly recommend the Norelco PT730.This allows you to use it plugged in at a much further distance from the wall.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I cannot yet speak to charge times or usage time but it seems as though the stated 8 hours charge and 40 minute usage are about right.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you&#x27;re a bald guy who needs a steady solution to shaving your head, I highly recommend the Norelco PT730.</li>

    <li> This review compares the Philips Norelco PT730 shaver to the Braun Series 1-190 shaver. I suspect that my comments will apply generally to most vibrating-blade shavers (e.g., Braun)  and rotating-blade shavers (e.g., Norelco).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve owned three of the Braun shavers (essentially identical) over the past six years. It would be very difficult to find a more ergonomic electric shaver. They charge quickly and hold charge a long time. About six months ago, I bought the Norelco shaver. It is not nearly as ergonomic as the Braun and does not charge nearly as fast and probably does not hold a charge as long. But the rotating-blade Norelco shaver is quiet and vibration-free, and its shave is a little closer. The Braun works best when the whiskers are short (best if the growth is no older than two days). The Norelco is better on the longer whiskers. I vacillate between the two shavers depending on my mood, whisker length, and perhaps other subconscious factors. I usually use both shavers to complete one shave. The Braun is best for straight edges like sideburns. My recommendation would be to buy both of these shavers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Even though the Braun is more ergonomic, I find as time goes by that I&#x27;m using the Norelco shaver more often than the Braun. The Braun shaver has one serious deficiency: The pop-up trimmer on all three of my Braun shavers quit working after a while (I can&#x27;t remember how long they worked). Not having this trimmer at hand is inconvenient, but I can use the pop-up trimmer on the Norelco.</li>

    <li> I was given the opportunity through Amazon Vine to review two of Norelco&#x27;s mid-range electric shavers - the PT720 and the PT730. At first glance, they seem to be identical except for color and the pop-up trimmer on this one (PT730) and the $10 price difference at this writing. However, upon use I find that there is indeed a difference in the way they shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Both shavers allow you to use them corded or cordless and both shavers can be rinsed clean under water. (You could actually use these razors in the shower, but rotary shavers perform better on a dry beard.) Both shavers feature the same, replaceable, flexing heads - which are amazing in their ability to follow the curves of your face while giving you a close shave. Both shavers last about 40 minutes on a single charge and both have an indicator light for battery status.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The differences are that this shaver features Super Lift &amp; Cut (which picks up longer hairs and shaves them smoothly), DualPrecision (which lets you shave even the shortest stubble cleanly), and a pop-up trimmer. The PT720 features Comfort Cut, which gives a gentler shave.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In trying both on my husband and sons, I found that for my husband, who has a heavy beard, this shaver gave him a closer shave than the PT720 on his 5 o&#x27;clock shadow. For one son, who is in college and shaves infrequently, this shaver picked up the long, scraggly hairs much, much better than the PT720. However, for another son with a heavy beard but very sensitive skin, the PT720 was much more comfortable and he said he would ONLY use that one. I was shocked to see such a big difference because the two shavers really do look identical.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The pop-up trimmer works great and I like that it is long enough to use without catching your head hair in the razor head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Clean up is just one press of a button and the head pops open. Then you can rinse the whole thing under the tap! Very easy and convenient. Norelco recommends replacing the head every 12 months for optimum performance. Also included is a little cleaning brush and a plastic head cover to protect the heads between uses.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are looking for a mid-priced, electric rotary-style shaver without a lot of whistles and bells, I think you will be pleased with this shaver. If you have extremely sensitive skin, you might want to look at Norelco&#x27;s PT720.head every 12 months for optimum performance. Also included is a little cleaning brush and a plastic head cover to protect the heads between uses.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you are looking for a mid-priced, electric rotary-style shaver without a lot of whistles and bells, I think you will be pleased with this shaver. If you have extremely sensitive skin, you might want to look at Norelco&#x27;s PT720.</li>

    <li> As a lifelong Norelco electric razor user, my husband says that the Norelco PT730 Rechargeable Cordless/Cord Tripleheader Razor is one of the best he has ever used. Some may say that an electric razor does not shave as close as shaving with a manual blade razor and shaving cream. Some may enjoy the ritual that goes along with manual shaving. I think most men are mistaken. The Norelco PT730 gives an incredibly close and comfortable shave, easily matching the results of a wet razor shave. (As a wife, I can feel it, too!) He hated the mess of shaving cream and gel, constantly replacing dull razors and walking out of the bathroom with tiny bits of tissue covering a cut or two. (Not sexy!)     <li> I read a few reviews of this product before I bought it, and I agree with others who noted that the motor is slower than earlier Norelco models. The only reason I replaced the old XL is the battery wore out, and you cannot just replace the old rechargeable battery with a new one.  Norelco continues to build shavers with rechargeable batteries that are soldered into place, so that you can either send the shaver in for them to repair ($30 estimated) or if you dare, try to follow one of the many YouTube demonstrations of unsoldering and replacing a failed battery.  I considered doing this with my old shaver, but by the time I had bought an appropriate soldering iron and a replacement battery I would have as much into it as buying a new shaver.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The new shaver also has a soldered battery.  This is a classic example of planned obsolescence and is unconscionable in this second decade of the 21st century.  This is my main reason for the 3-star rating for a product that works like a 4-5 star . . . Boo-hiss, Norelco!!!</li>

    <li> This is a great shaver! My husband loves this kind and will not buy anything else. He&#x27;s had 2 in the 16 years I&#x27;ve been married to him and they seem to last a pretty long time.</li>
    <li> All the Norelco dry shavers \\&quot;work\\&quot; the same these days.  The old days of 5 lights or LCD screens or different colors and symbols are gone.  They now almost all use rechargeable batteries that don&#x27;t have the same useful life or power as the good old Ni-Cads I used to see last 10+ years (they now use either Li-Ion or NiMH, the NiMH seem to work better for me). The 6943 and other variations of cord only HQ56 shavers are gone, as are the 8100 and other HQ8/9 cord only models, or they are at ridiculous prices.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One version swivels, one version works wet and there are a few old left overs that basically do the same thing, but their batteries are aging as they have not been made for years.  So, unless you want to swivel or shave wet, it boils down to the difference between the current heads and here I am speaking of the HQ56 or the HQ8 or HQ9.  I have never used the RQ series and I never will.  I just don&#x27;t see the logic or buying an entire new head when you only need new blades, and $50 for blades each year is more than the entire price of the PT730.  So here it is, after shaving with Norelco for 45+ years with all the different heads.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The HQ56 are OK.  After you use them for a while, it takes a bit longer to get the thicker stubble and you have to go back over the same spot a little more.  They don&#x27;t seem to last a full year, but when they are new they do a decent job.  When they are cheap, and I mean $10 or so less than the HQ8/9 then they are a good deal and you won&#x27;t mind when the shaver batteries die in 3-4 years because the shaver was cheap as well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;However, if you use the HQ56 for a while and then go to the HQ8/9 you will think a barber moved into your bathroom and just gave you a custom shave.  Not only that, you will find that it takes quite a bit less time, almost half.  I have yet to feel a significant difference between the HQ8 and HQ9, probably because they do different things better.  The HQ8 has fewer cutters and a few largerholes for longer hairs and the HQ9 has more holes and a system of concentric cutters for a faster shave.  Cutter count is not the only thing that makes a difference though.  The old fashioned HQ56 has nearly twice the cutters of the HQ8 and the HQ8 does a better job.  I mix them (HQ8 and 9)on a single shaver as I have yet to decide which I like best.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, in the HQ8/9 heads, the PT730 is the best deal.  Also, rather important, the 730 keeps the blade speed up when it is on batteries.  When Norelco switched to the newer batteries and dumped the Ni-cads (EU regulations) the early models had a big problem keeping the speed up after a few minutes of shaving.  If you wanted the fastest blade rotation, you had to use a cord.  A 50 minute battery life is pretty worthless when the shave stinks after 10 minutes because the blades are too slow.  This latest version seems to have fixed this issue pretty well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In the HQ56 heads, the 6948XL is the best deal.  If you want to save some money and you aren&#x27;t picky or in a hurry, the 6948XL will do the trick.  The 6948XL is made in China and the fit and finish are not as good as the shavers made in Holland.  However, I have had the newer Chinese shavers apart and the quality of the electronics is good.  So if the extra cost is not a problem, by all means enjoy the PT730.  And though it doesn&#x27;t matter as much these days, the 730 is made in China as well.  Looks like the 830 is the only model in this series still made in Holland.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Just a quick note for anyone interested.  It looks as though all the wet shavers will now only work cordless.  Not a big problem, but for those of us who count on corded use, be aware.  And watch for a better price near Christmas.</li>

    <li> I have been through several electric razors, and I&#x27;m a fairly slow buyer, using my razors until they croak. It is not as easy nor as convenient to engage. With my old one, I could just flip the razor in my hand; my thumb would just naturally come to rest on the mechanism, which I could engage by just pushing forward by straightening out my thumb. With this new one, after flipping the razor over, I have to work my way up towards the head, find the latch mechanism with my thumb, then pull it down. by flexing my thumb, to free the trimmer to pop out.&lt;br /&gt;These seem like minor details, but they add up to just an &amp;#34;Okay&amp;#34; experience, after my old one. While it may give the illusion of having less power than the old 5801XL I&#x27;ve been using, probably because it is so much quieter, it gives me an even closer shave than the 5801XL in about the same amount of time.  There is also a notable difference in how much better it handles the thicker/more stubborn hairs.  I&#x27;m guessing that has a lot to do with the new head design allowing for different size hairs.  I would constantly have to use the hair trimmer accessory with the 5801XL to get those hairs, but have so for not had to do it with this one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I also like how much easier it is to clean the head and also the ability to wash it under running water.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, as compared to the 5801XL that I have been so happy with over the years, I think this one is definitely a step up.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update 2/17/2013: With daily use from a full charge, the battery lasted a good two months! Goes much longer between charges than my older model, even before it started not to hold as much charge.&lt;br /&gt;It&#x27;s funny - every time I get a new Norelco, it sounds different than the previous models.&lt;br /&gt;Shaves nicely, trims nicely.&lt;br /&gt;Only caveat: Don&#x27;t judge it after the first charge.  The first charge didn&#x27;t last all that long and I thought I was going to be disappointed; however, the very next charge has lasted and lasted.&lt;br /&gt;Only negative: It didn&#x27;t come with any kind of stand, and the shape is slightly different from my last one, so the stand I&#x27;m keeping it in leaves me a bit unsure.  Will it tip over?  SO...I keep the travel cap on the blades in case it falls.  Almost every time I go to remove the cap, the blades spring open because the release is right at the front of the blade unit.  If it came with its own storage stand, it would be five-star rating.</li>
    <li> This replaced an old Norelco electric razor with a trimmer that died after ten plus years.  I was shocked at how light and cheap feeling this new razor was.  However, when I shaved my neck and face, I was impressed at how good a job it did.  Unfortunately, the trimming function was the main reason I purchased this razor and it is very poorly designed.  Compared to my previous razor, which had a solid metal slide to open and close the trimmer, this trimmer is as cheap as they come.  Further, the angle of the trimmer is almost 90 degrees to the razor vs 45 degrees from my older razor.  At 90 degrees, the razor gets in the way so you cannot see very well to trim your beard and moustache.  The off/on button is hard to find and push as is the trimmer button.  Also the button does not close the trimmer as before.  The trimmer function is hugely inferior and not recommended although the shave is good.  For my purposes, I would not buy again.</li>
    <li> This is my third Norelco electric razor, all of which have had long service lives. I like the PT730 the best so far because of the close shave it delivers at such a low cost. The dual precision cutting heads make this razor stand out in performance over previous Norelco razors. I held a star back because I have only had it for a few months.</li>
    <li> I purchased it at least a month or two ago. It works better if you shave without lotion on your body, when you legs are dry. However, it takes a few rounds to get almost all the hair off. However, for the price it&#x27;s ok for now.</li>
    <li> This Powertouch Electric Razor  is very cheap. And it use very easy. It can wash by water. But it can not clear by water only</li>
    <li> Razor performs as expected - close cut, smooth cut, trims easily, charges and indicates full charge visibly and cleans with little effort.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only negative is the charging cord. The female plug doesn&#x27;t fit  tightly and pulls out frequently which is annoying! Other than that it would have received a five star rating.</li>
